<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_national_football_team" title="Djibouti national football team">French Somaliland</a> 2–10 <strong class="selflink">Ethiopia</strong><span class="flagicon"> <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></span><br/>
(<a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>; May 5, 1954)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rating_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-rating-3">[3]</a></sup></td>
</tr>

<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Biggest defeat</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Flag_of_Iraq_%281991-2004%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Iraq_%281991-2004%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Flag_of_Iraq_%281991-2004%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Iraq_%281991-2004%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Flag_of_Iraq_%281991-2004%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Iraq_%281991-2004%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Iraq_national_football_team" title="Iraq national football team">Iraq</a></span> 13–0 <strong class="selflink">Ethiopia</strong><span class="flagicon"> <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281975%E2%80%931987%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281975%E2%80%931987%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281975%E2%80%931987%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281975%E2%80%931987%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281975%E2%80%931987%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281975%E2%80%931987%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></span><br/>
(<a href="/wiki/Irbid" title="Irbid">Irbid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>; 18 August 1992)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rating_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-rating-3">[3]</a></sup></td>

<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Appearances</th>
<td>10 (<i>first in <a href="/wiki/1957_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1957 African Cup of Nations">1957</a></i>)</td>
</tr>

<th scope="row">Best result</th>
<td>Champions, <a href="/wiki/1962_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1962 African Cup of Nations">1962</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">This article contains several <a href="/wiki/Patronymic" title="Patronymic">patronymic</a> names. These persons are addressed by their <a href="/wiki/Given_name" title="Given name">given name</a>, and not by their <a href="/wiki/Naming_conventions_in_Ethiopia_and_Eritrea" title="Naming conventions in Ethiopia and Eritrea">inherited name</a>.</div>
<p>The <b>Ethiopia national football team</b>—nicknamed "<b>Walias,</b>" after the <a href="/wiki/Walia_ibex" title="Walia ibex">Walia ibex</a>, represents <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> and is presided over by the <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Football_Federation" title="Ethiopian Football Federation">Ethiopian Football Federation</a>, the governing body for <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Ethiopia" title="Football in Ethiopia">football in Ethiopia</a>. The team has been representing Ethiopia in regional, continental, and international competitions since its founding in 1943.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EFFIFA_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-EFFIFA-4">[4]</a></sup> The Walias play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa_Stadium" title="Addis Ababa Stadium">Addis Ababa Stadium</a> located in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They are currently ranked 112th in the world according to the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a> and 34th in <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">CAF</a><sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ranking_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-ranking-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Since May 2016,<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the team is led by <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_manager" title="Caretaker manager">caretaker manager</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gebremedhin_Haile&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gebremedhin Haile (page does not exist)">Gebremedhin Haile</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yohannes-out_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yohannes-out-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ethiopia was one of only three teams (along with <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sudan_national_football_team" title="Sudan national football team">Sudan</a>) to participate in the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1957_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="1957 Africa Cup of Nations">1957</a>. It won the competition in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1962_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="1962 Africa Cup of Nations">1962</a> and while it was also the host. However, success has been elusive since the end of the 1960s. Under a previous coach <a href="/wiki/Sewnet_Bishaw" title="Sewnet Bishaw">Sewnet Bishaw</a>, the team qualified for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="2013 African Cup of Nations">2013 African Cup of Nations</a> after a 31-year absence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EFFIFA_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-EFFIFA-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ethiopia has a long football tradition and was among the pioneers of international competition in Africa, playing its first international match in 1947, defeating <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_national_football_team" title="Djibouti national football team">French Somaliland</a> 5–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rating_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-rating-3">[3]</a></sup> The EFF joined <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> in 1952<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EFFIFA_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-EFFIFA-4">[4]</a></sup> and was one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">Confederation of African Football</a> in 1957.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The team took part in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1957_African_Nations_Cup" title="1957 African Nations Cup">inaugural African Nations Cup</a> in 1957, where it finished second.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In 1959, Ethiopia entered the <a href="/wiki/1962_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA_%E2%80%93_Group_7)" title="1962 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA – Group 7)">1962 World Cup qualification</a> for the first time and faced <a href="/wiki/Israel_national_football_team" title="Israel national football team">Israel</a> in the second round after a bye. The team lost both games; and with an aggregate score of 2–4 was knocked out of the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The team won the African tournament on home soil, in 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Nine countries entered the competition, including the reigning champions <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">United Arab Republic</a>, meaning for the first time a qualification tournament was required. As with previous tournaments, the finals only included four teams. <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">United Arab Republic</a>, as holders, and Ethiopia as hosts, qualified automatically meaning each needed to play only one game to reach the final. Ethiopia won the tournament for the first time after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_time" title="Extra time">extra time</a> in the final. <a href="/wiki/Mengistu_Worku" title="Mengistu Worku">Mengistu Worku</a> and <a href="/wiki/Badawi_Abdel_Fattah" title="Badawi Abdel Fattah">Badawi Abdel Fattah</a> were joint top-scorers, both with three goals each, but the award itself was given to Worku because his team had won the title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lost_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-lost-11">[11]</a></sup> This was the greatest feat ever achieved by the Ethiopian National team, and the only African Cup of Nations title it has ever won. <a href="/wiki/Luciano_Vassalo" title="Luciano Vassalo">Luciano Vassalo</a> was the team's captain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghana_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ghana-12">[12]</a></sup> and the coach was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ydnekatchew_Tessema" title="Ydnekatchew Tessema">Ydnekatchew Tessema</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1963_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1963 African Cup of Nations">1963 African Cup of Nations</a> they finished fourth, after losing the third place battle against <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">United Arab Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1965_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1965 African Cup of Nations">1965 African Cup of Nations</a> was even more of a disappointment for Ethiopia, as national team was eliminated in group phase by <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_national_football_team" title="Tunisia national football team">Tunisia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team" title="Senegal national football team">Senegal</a>, finishing at the bottom of the group, with only one scored goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Next African Cup of Nations was in 1968, again on home soil, and the team won third place after losing to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_DR_national_football_team" title="Congo DR national football team">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> in the semifinals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> But two years later, the team went through a real disaster, as they finished at the bottom of the group phase, with a goal difference of 3–12.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The worse was yet to come for Ethiopia as they didn't qualify for the <a href="/wiki/1972_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1972 African Cup of Nations">1972 African Cup of Nations</a> at all, losing to <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_football_team" title="Kenya national football team">Kenya</a> in the qualifying tournament with a 0–3 aggregate.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Almost the same thing happened for the <a href="/wiki/1974_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1974 African Cup of Nations">1974 African Cup of Nations</a>. This time they were eliminated by <a href="/wiki/Tanzania_national_football_team" title="Tanzania national football team">Tanzania</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Ethiopia hosted the Nations Cup tournament in 1976, but failed to progress to the final four, finishing third in the group, behind <a href="/wiki/Guinea_national_football_team" title="Guinea national football team">Guinea</a> and Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In 1977, they played <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_national_football_team" title="Mauritius national football team">Mauritius</a> in the qualifiers for the <a href="/wiki/1978_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1978 African Cup of Nations">1978 African Cup of Nations</a>. After 4–2 win on aggregate, they had to play <a href="/wiki/Uganda_national_football_team" title="Uganda national football team">Uganda</a>. After 0–0 tie from the first match, Uganda won the second match, 2–1, and progressed to the final tournament.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They also missed <a href="/wiki/1980_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1980 African Cup of Nations">1980 African Cup of Nations</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Ethiopia last qualified for the tournament in 1982, under coach <a href="/wiki/Mengistu_Worku" title="Mengistu Worku">Mengistu Worku</a>, legendary former player. They failed to make it past the groups stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_history">Later history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Later history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Earlier_success_in_CECAFA_Cup_.282001.E2.80.932007.29">Earlier success in CECAFA Cup (2001–2007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Earlier success in CECAFA Cup (2001–2007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/CECAFA_Cup" title="CECAFA Cup">CECAFA Cup</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2001_CECAFA_Cup" title="2001 CECAFA Cup">2001 CECAFA Cup</a>, Ethiopia beat <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_national_football_team" title="Zanzibar national football team">Zanzibar</a> 5–0<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and tied 1–1 with <a href="/wiki/Rwanda_national_football_team" title="Rwanda national football team">Rwanda B</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> to advance to the quarterfinals against <a href="/wiki/Burundi_national_football_team" title="Burundi national football team">Burundi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> After a 2–2 tie in regulation, they beat Burundi 5–4 in penalty kicks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Ethiopia went on to beat <a href="/wiki/Rwanda_national_football_team" title="Rwanda national football team">Rwanda A</a> 1–0<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> in the semi-finals and <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_football_team" title="Kenya national football team">Kenya</a> 2–1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> in the finals to win the championship for the first time since 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Because of their success in 2001 with <a href="/wiki/Asrat_Haile" title="Asrat Haile">Asrat Haile</a> at the helm, Ethiopia jumped 17 spots in <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA rankings</a> from 155th to 138th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Despite their success, the EFF chose to replace Asrat with <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Jochen_Figge" title="Jochen Figge">Jochen Figge</a> in August 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2002_CECAFA_Cup" title="2002 CECAFA Cup">2002 CECAFA Cup</a>, Ethiopia failed to qualify past the group stage of the competition; they lost all four of their games against Zanzibar,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Uganda_national_football_team" title="Uganda national football team">Uganda</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Somalia_national_football_team" title="Somalia national football team">Somalia</a>, and Rwanda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/2003_CECAFA_Cup" title="2003 CECAFA Cup">2003 CECAFA Cup</a>, Ethiopia withdrew just before the start of the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The competition only had six participating countries with Burundi, Djibouti, Somalia, and <a href="/wiki/Tanzania_national_football_team" title="Tanzania national football team">Tanzania</a> also choosing not to participate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The EFF fired Figge in May 2003, even though the team had won two games and was second in their group in the <a href="/wiki/2004_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="2004 African Cup of Nations">2004 African Cup of Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/2004_African_Cup_of_Nations_qualification" title="2004 African Cup of Nations qualification">qualifiers</a>. Then assistant coach, Asrat was appointed interim coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Ethiopia failed to qualify by 3 points with a loss in the final game in <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Asrat was soon replaced by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Seyoum_Kebede&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Seyoum Kebede (page does not exist)">Seyoum Kebede</a> whose tenure with the "Walias" was also short lived.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The next challenge was the <a href="/wiki/2004_CECAFA_Cup" title="2004 CECAFA Cup">2004 CECAFA Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>. There were 9 teams in regional tournament: Burundi, Zanzibar, Rwanda, Ethiopia, Tanzania, Sudan, Kenya, Uganda and Somalia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2004_Cecafa_Cup_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-2004_Cecafa_Cup-35">[35]</a></sup> Ethiopia was led by captain <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zewdu_Bekele&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zewdu Bekele (page does not exist)">Zewdu Bekele</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and again by coach Asrat who was recalled to the position a mere two weeks before the beginning of the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> After defeating Burundi, tying with Rwanda and beating Tanzania, and Zanzibar, the team advanced to the semi-finals for the first time since 2001. Ethiopia advanced to the championship after a dramatic nail-biting penalty shootout with Kenya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2004_Cecafa_Cup_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-2004_Cecafa_Cup-35">[35]</a></sup> The team went on to beat Burundi 3–0 and win the 2004 CECAFA Cup on Dec 25, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> That night, people all across Addis Ababa sang and danced in the streets.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The Ethiopian national team was the champion of the same <a href="/wiki/CECAFA_Cup" title="CECAFA Cup">CECAFA Cup</a> competition again in <a href="/wiki/2005_CECAFA_Cup" title="2005 CECAFA Cup">2005</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Kigali" title="Kigali">Kigali</a>, Rwanda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> This time coached by <a href="/wiki/Sewnet_Bishaw" title="Sewnet Bishaw">Sewnet Bishaw</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>—after a 0–0 draw with Uganda and a 3–1 victory over Sudan—Ethiopia thrashed <a href="/wiki/Djibouti_national_football_team" title="Djibouti national football team">Djibouti</a> in a 6–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> They then went on to beat Somalia 3–1. Semi-finals saw Ethiopia whip Zanzibar 4–0, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fikru_Tefera" title="Fikru Tefera">Fikru Tefera</a> scoring a hat-trick. In the final match, <a href="/wiki/Andualem_Negusse" title="Andualem Negusse">Andualem Negusse's</a> goal allowed Ethiopia to take the cup again with a 1–0 win over Rwanda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Ethiopian team did not fare as well in the next three appearances at the CECAFA Cup. At the <a href="/wiki/2006_CECAFA_Cup" title="2006 CECAFA Cup">2006 CECAFA Cup</a> in Addis Ababa, Ethiopia lost to Tanzania<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> but beat Djibouti and Malawi in the group stage to advance to the quarterfinals against Zambia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> They lost 0–1 with a very late goal by Zambia's <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Sakuwaha" title="Jonas Sakuwaha">Jonas Sakuwaha</a> in the 87th minute of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> On Dec 6, a <a href="/wiki/CECAFA" title="CECAFA">CECAFA</a> emergency committee made the extraordinary decision to have the match replayed because referee <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Issa_Kagabi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Issa Kagabi (page does not exist)">Issa Kagabi</a> (Rwanda) supposedly had whistled the end of the match prematurely. Zambia announced they would refuse to play Ethiopia again. CECAFA secretary general <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nicholas_Musonye&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nicholas Musonye (page does not exist)">Nicholas Musonye</a>—not present at the emergency committee meeting—threatened that he'd cancel the entire tournament should match be replayed. <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Football_Federation" title="Ethiopian Football Federation">Ethiopian Football Federation</a> declined to have the match replayed and graciously withdrew from the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/2007_CECAFA_Cup" title="2007 CECAFA Cup">2007 CECAFA Cup</a>, Ethiopia suffered a 1–3 loss to Zanzibar and a hard-fought 0–0 draw with Sudan in which they failed to produce a goal despite star <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fikru_Tefera" title="Fikru Tefera">Fikru Tefera</a>'s call up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> This was enough to eliminate Ethiopia from the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>

<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. </tr>
</table>
<p>Being kicked out of the tournament early, the young and inexperienced Ethiopian squad faced a more uncertain future.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Suspension_and_reinstatement_.282008.E2.80.932009.29">Suspension and reinstatement (2008–2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Suspension and reinstatement (2008–2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the 2008 African Cup of Nations qualifiers, Ethiopia finished bottom of their group after losing their last two games.</p>
<p>In July 2008, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_Emergency_Committee" title="FIFA Emergency Committee">FIFA Emergency Committee</a> decided to suspend the <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Football_Federation" title="Ethiopian Football Federation">Ethiopian Football Federation</a> (EFF) due to their failure to comply with the road map to normalize the federation agreed upon in February 2008 by <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">CAF</a> and EFF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The road map was established in Feb 2008 following the dismissal of the country's football federation president <a href="/wiki/Ashebir_Woldegiorgis" title="Ashebir Woldegiorgis">Ashebir Woldegiorgis</a> by the countries authorities. One of the main points of the road map was the organization of an "extraordinary general assembly" to deal with the "motion of dismissal". In addition, the EFF offices were to be handed over to the recognized leadership of the federation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The suspension of the EFF came into force on July 29, 2008, the day on which the federation had officially been notified of its suspension. Ethiopia played four group level matches in <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(CAF)" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification (CAF)">2010 FIFA World Cup qualification</a> before FIFA announced the immediate suspension of the Ethiopian Football Federation. On September 12, 2008, FIFA excluded the Ethiopian team from the 2010 World Cup qualifiers and the results of their matches were cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Ethiopia's exclusion from the World Cup also led to their exclusion from the Africa Cup of Nations. While it was not clear if the team was also explicitly excluded from the <a href="/wiki/2010_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2010 Africa Cup of Nations">2010 Africa Cup of Nations</a>, their failure to complete the remaining fixtures effectively eliminated them from the tournament because the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualification was also used to determine the qualification for 2010 Africa Cup of Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The team also missed the <a href="/wiki/2008_CECAFA_Cup" title="2008 CECAFA Cup">2008 CECAFA Cup</a> due to this suspension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2009, the EFF was reinstated after organizing the extraordinary general assembly and electing new leaders as instructed by FIFA. FIFA's executive committee had voted a month before to lift the suspension so long as that EFF organized and chaired an elective general assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> FIFA confirmed that it was satisfied with the election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_troubles_.282009.E2.80.932011.29">Continued troubles (2009–2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Continued troubles (2009–2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2009_CECAFA_Cup" title="2009 CECAFA Cup">2009 CECAFA Cup</a>, Ethiopia defeated Djibouti 5–0,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> but lost 0–1 to <a href="/wiki/Zambia_national_football_team" title="Zambia national football team">Zambia</a> and 0–2 to <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_football_team" title="Kenya national football team">Kenya</a>, thus finishing third in the group and getting eliminated from the regional tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2010_CECAFA_Cup" title="2010 CECAFA Cup">2010 CECAFA Cup</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, Ethiopia was in Group C with <a href="/wiki/Uganda_national_football_team" title="Uganda national football team">Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_football_team" title="Kenya national football team">Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malawi_national_football_team" title="Malawi national football team">Malawi</a>. After the 1–2 loss to Uganda,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Ethiopia beat Kenya 2–1 and came to a 1–1 draw with Malawi. Next opponent was Zambia, and Ethiopia won 2–1 by two goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In semi-finals however, they lost to Ivory Coast 0–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In the third-place battle to follow, they lost 3–4 to Uganda to come in fourth place in the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Tournament's star players and goal scorers were <a href="/wiki/Shimelis_Bekele" title="Shimelis Bekele">Shimelis Bekele</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Awassa_City_FC" title="Awassa City FC">Awassa City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oumed_Oukri" title="Oumed Oukri">Oumed Oukri</a> of <a href="/wiki/Defence_Force_F.C." title="Defence Force F.C.">Defence Force</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The team had exceeded fans’ expectations by reaching the semi-final stage.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In April 2011, the Ethiopian Football Federation fired national coach <a href="/wiki/Iffy_Onuora" title="Iffy Onuora">Iffy Onuora</a> – just 9 months after he took charge of the Ethiopian national football team. Ethiopian Football Federation cited disciplinary grounds for his dismissal just a month after the team's 4–0 defeat at the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigerian Green Eagles</a> in Group B of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2012 Africa Cup of Nations">2012 Africa Cup of Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/2012_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_qualification#Group_B" title="2012 Africa Cup of Nations qualification">qualification</a> in <a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iffy_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-iffy-64">[64]</a></sup> The Ethiopian national team had played 11 matches during coach Onuora's tenure, winning 4, drawing in 1 and losing 6 matches. The team scored 12 goals and conceded 21 goals in those matches.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In May 2011, the EFF appointed former <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_national_football_team" title="Zimbabwe national football team">Zimbabwe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_football_team" title="Namibia national football team">Namibia</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Tom_Saintfiet" title="Tom Saintfiet">Tom Saintfiet</a> as coach in place of Iffy Onuora.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saintfiet-in_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-saintfiet-in-65">[65]</a></sup> However, Tom Saintfiet left his job as Ethiopia's national soccer coach after just five months, citing "broken promises" as the reason for his departure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saintfiet-out_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-saintfiet-out-66">[66]</a></sup> Saintfiet had been in charge for three 2012 African Cup of Nations qualification matches, including a 2–2 draw with <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a> that contributed to the Super Eagles missing out on 2012 Africa Cup of Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saintfiet-out_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-saintfiet-out-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_successes">Recent successes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Recent successes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_African_Cup_of_Nations">2013 African Cup of Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2013 African Cup of Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualification">Qualification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Qualification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_qualification" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations qualification">2013 Africa Cup of Nations qualification</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_qualification" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations qualification">qualification</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations">2013 Africa Cup of Nations</a>, Ethiopia tied 1–1 with Benin after a goalless draw in the first leg at home to progress to the last round of qualification because of the <a href="/wiki/Away_goals_rule" title="Away goals rule">away goals rule</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In the last round of qualification, Ethiopia came to a 5–5 draw in aggregate score against Sudan, but passed to the championships again due to the away goals rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> This is the first time that Ethiopia has qualified to the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a> in 31 years, and it opens a new chapter in Ethiopian sports history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_World_Cup_qualification">2014 World Cup qualification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2014 World Cup qualification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(CAF)" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification (CAF)">2014 FIFA World Cup qualification (CAF)</a></div>
<p>The Ethiopian national soccer team advanced to the CAF group stage of the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> with a 5–0 aggregate victory over <a href="/wiki/Somalia_national_football_team" title="Somalia national football team">Somalia</a>. Ethiopia joined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_African_national_football_team" title="South African national football team">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botswana_national_football_team" title="Botswana national football team">Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_national_football_team" title="Central African Republic national football team">Central African Republic</a> (CAR) in <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_CAF_Second_Round#Group_A" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification – CAF Second Round">Group A</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>

<p><b>Ethiopia</b> won 5–0 on aggregate and advanced to the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_CAF_Second_Round" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification – CAF Second Round">Second Round</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_A">Group A</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Group A">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_CAF_Second_Round" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification – CAF Second Round">2014 FIFA World Cup qualification – CAF Second Round</a></div>
<p>Ethiopia tied with South Africa away from home 1–1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> and beat <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">CAR</a> at home 2–0<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> to top the group after the first two games. They beat <a href="/wiki/Botswana_national_football_team" title="Botswana national football team">Botswana</a> twice, 1–0 on Mar 22, 2013 at home in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a> and 2–1 on Jun 7 in <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>. However, the Jun 7 win was later awarded to Botswana by a score of 3–0 after it was discovered that Ethiopia fielded an ineligible player. They beat South Africa 2–1 on Jun 14 at home and secured Ethiopian advancement to the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_CAF_Third_Round" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification – CAF Third Round">third round</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qual_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-qual-75">[74]</a></sup> The team eventually was eliminated by <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a> with two defeats in the Third Round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-profile_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-profile-76">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p><br/></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dd><b><a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a> :</b>
<dl>
<dd>
<ul>
<li>1 time Champion (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1962_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="1962 Africa Cup of Nations">1962</a>)</li>
<li>1 time runners-up (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1957_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="1957 Africa Cup of Nations">1957</a>)</li>
<li>1 time third-place finish (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1959_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="1959 Africa Cup of Nations">1959</a>)</li>
<li>2 time fourth-place finish (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1963_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="1963 Africa Cup of Nations">1963</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1968_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="1968 Africa Cup of Nations">1968</a>)</li>
</ul>
</dd>
</dl>
</dd>
<dd><b><a href="/wiki/CECAFA_Cup" title="CECAFA Cup">CECAFA Cup</a> :</b>
<dl>
<dd>
<ul>
<li>4 times Champion (<a href="/wiki/1987_CECAFA_Cup" title="1987 CECAFA Cup">1987</a>, <a href="/wiki/2001_CECAFA_Cup" title="2001 CECAFA Cup">2001</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004_CECAFA_Cup" title="2004 CECAFA Cup">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_CECAFA_Cup" title="2005 CECAFA Cup">2005</a>)</li>
<li>2 time third-place finish (<a href="/wiki/2000_CECAFA_Cup" title="2000 CECAFA Cup">2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_CECAFA_Cup" title="2015 CECAFA Cup">2015</a>)</li>
<li>2 time fourth-place finish (<a href="/wiki/1995_CECAFA_Cup" title="1995 CECAFA Cup">1995</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_CECAFA_Cup" title="2010 CECAFA Cup">2010</a>)</li>
</ul>
</dd>
</dl>
</dd>
</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethiopia_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-Somalia-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Somalia_72-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Due to the lack of security in Mogadishu, Somalia's home game was played at a neutral venue. An earlier Somali request for the match to be played in <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a> was rejected by FIFA due to a ban on international matches being played in <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-botswana-ethiopia-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-botswana-ethiopia_78-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">FIFA awarded Botswana a 3–0 win as a result of Ethiopia fielding the ineligible player <a href="/wiki/Minyahil_Teshome" title="Minyahil Teshome">Minyahil Teshome</a>. The match originally ended 2–1 to Ethiopia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<div id="Africa_Cup_of_Nations_.C2.B7_Champions" style="font-size:114%"><a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a> · Champions</div>

<tr>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px;background:transparent;color:inherit;">
<div style="padding:0px;">
<table class="navbox-columns-table" style="border-spacing: 0px; text-align:left;width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
<tr style="vertical-align:top;">
<td style="width:2.4em;">   </td>
<td style="padding:0px;;;;width:24em;">
<div>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/1957_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1957 African Cup of Nations">1957</a>:</b> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Flag_of_Egypt_%281952-1958%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Egypt_%281952-1958%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Flag_of_Egypt_%281952-1958%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Egypt_%281952-1958%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Flag_of_Egypt_%281952-1958%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Egypt_%281952-1958%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">Egypt</a></span><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1959_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1959 African Cup of Nations">1959</a>:</b> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Republic.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Republic.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Republic.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Republic.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_United_Arab_Republic.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">United Arab Republic</a></span><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1962_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1962 African Cup of Nations">1962</a>:</b> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ethiopia_%281897-1936%3B_1941-1974%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><strong class="selflink">Ethiopia</strong></span><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1963_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1963 African Cup of Nations">1963</a>:</b> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Ghana.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ghana.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Ghana.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ghana.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Ghana.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ghana.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team" title="Ghana national football team">Ghana</a></span><br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1965_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1965 African Cup of Nations">1965</a>:</b> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana"><img alt="Ghana" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Ghana.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ghana.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Ghana.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ghana.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Ghana.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ghana.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> Ghana<br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/1968_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1968 African Cup of Nations">1968</a>:</b> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="496" data-file-width="744" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Flag_of_Congo-Kinshasa_%281966-1971%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Congo-Kinshasa_%281966-1971%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Flag_of_Congo-Kinshasa_%281966-1971%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Congo-Kinshasa_%281966-1971%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Flag_of_Congo-Kinshasa_%281966-1971%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Congo-Kinshasa_%281966-1971%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/DR_Congo_national_football_team" title="DR Congo national football team">Congo-Kinshasa</a></span></p>
</div>
</td>
<td style="border-left:2px solid #fdfdfd;padding:0px;;;;width:24em;">
